6\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Total fatalities\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         433 total\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th </a>\n          season on record)\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #CFCFCF;">\n         Related articles\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="text-align: left;">\n          <ul>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season">\n             Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/2017_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2017 Pacific hurricane season">\n             2017 Pacific hurricane season\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/2017_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2017 Pacific typhoon season">\n             2017 Pacific typhoon season\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <a href="/wiki/2017_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season" title="2017 North Indian Ocean cyclone season">\n             2017 North Indian Ocean cyclone season\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">\n          Atlantic hurricane seasons\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          2015\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">\n          2016\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <b>\n          2017\n         </b>\n         ,\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">\n           2018\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">\n           2019\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        2017 Atlantic hurricane season\n       </b>\n       is an ongoing event in the annual formation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclones\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_basin" title="Atlantic basin">\n        Atlantic basin\n       </a>\n       . The season has been hyperactive,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       featuring 17 named storms, making it tied with\n       <a href="/wiki/1936_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1936 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1936\n       </a>\n       as the fifth-most active season since reliable records began in 1851 and featuring both the highest total\n       <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">\n        accumulated cyclone energy\n       </a>\n       (ACE) and the highest number of major hurricanes since\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        the 2005 season\n       </a>\n       . It has the greatest number of consecutive hurricanes in the satellite era, with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Franklin_(2017)" title="Hurricane Franklin (2017)">\n        Franklin\n       </a>\n       through\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">\n        Ophelia\n       </a>\n       all reaching winds of at least 75\xc2\xa0mph (120\xc2\xa0km/h). In addition, it is most destructive season on record, with a preliminary total of over $316.51 billion (\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_states_dollar" title="United states dollar">\n        USD\n       </a>\n       ) in damages, nearly all of which was due to three of the major hurricanes of the season \xe2\x80\x94\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Harvey\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">\n        Irma\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">\n        Maria\n       </a>\n       . This season is also\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes#Systems" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">\n        one of only six years\n       </a>\n       on record to feature multiple Category\xc2\xa05 hurricanes. Irma\'s landfalls on multiple\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">\n        Caribbean\n       </a>\n       islands and Maria\'s landfall on\n       <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">\n        Dominica\n       </a>\n       make 2017 the second season on record (after\n       <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2007\n       </a>\n       ) to feature two hurricanes making landfall at Category\xc2\xa05 intensity. In addition, Irma was the strongest hurricane ever recorded to form in the Atlantic Ocean outside of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">\n        Caribbean Sea\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This season is the only season on record in which three hurricanes each had an\n       <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">\n        ACE\n       </a>\n       of over 40:\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">\n        Irma\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">\n        Jose\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">\n        Maria\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The season officially began on June\xc2\xa01 and will end on November\xc2\xa030. These dates historically describe the period of year when most tropical cyclones form in the Atlantic basin and are adopted by convention. However, as shown by\n       <a href="#Tropical_Storm_Arlene">\n        Tropical Storm Arlene\n       </a>\n       in April, the formation of tropical cyclones is possible at other times of the year. Arlene also marked 2017 the third consecutive year to feature a pre-season storm. In mid-June,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">\n        Tropical Storm Bret\n       </a>\n       struck the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">\n        Trinidad\n       </a>\n       , which is only rarely struck by tropical cyclones due to its low latitude. A few days later,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">\n        Tropical Storm Cindy\n       </a>\n       struck the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       . In late August,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Hurricane Harvey\n       </a>\n       became the first major hurricane to make landfall in the United States since\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Wilma\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2005\n       </a>\n       , while also setting the record for the costliest tropical cyclone on record, as well as the most rainfall dropped by a tropical cyclone in the US. In early September,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">\n        Hurricane Irma\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_hurricane" title="Cape Verde hurricane">\n        Cape Verde-type hurricane\n       </a>\n       , became the first\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Category_5_hurricane" title="Category 5 hurricane">\n        Category 5\xc2\xa0hurricane\n       </a>\n       to impact the northern\n       <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">\n        Leeward Islands\n       </a>\n       on record, as well as equaling the strongest hurricane ever to make landfall in the Atlantic basin\xe2\x80\x94the\n       <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">\n        1935 Labor Day hurricane\n       </a>\n       . With\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">\n        Hurricane Maria\n       </a>\n       striking\n       <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">\n        Puerto Rico\n       </a>\n       as a high-end Category\xc2\xa04, the season was the first on record to feature three Atlantic hurricanes making landfall anywhere in the United States or one of its territories at Category\xc2\xa04 intensity or stronger. The season also featured the fastest tropical cyclone ever recorded in the Gulf of Mexico (\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nate_(2017)" title="Hurricane Nate (2017)">\n        Nate\n       </a>\n       ). This was the first season to have three hurricanes make landfall in the mainland United States (Harvey, Irma, and Nate) since\n       <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2008\n       </a>\n       , and the first season to feature four hurricanes making landfall in the overall United States (Harvey, Irma, Maria, and Nate) since\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2005\n       </a>\n       . The season also featured\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)">\n        Ophelia\n       </a>\n       , the easternmost major hurricane in the basin on record, which later became the costliest hurricane to affect the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">\n        United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">\n        Ireland\n       </a>\n       in history. For the first time since\n       <a href="/wiki/2013_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2013 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2013\n       </a>\n       , a named storm formed in every month of the season (June to November).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in 2017, the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">\n        National Hurricane Center\n       </a>\n       (NHC) has the option to issue advisories, and thus allow watches and warnings to be issued, on disturbances that are not yet tropical cyclones but have a high chance to become one, and are expected to bring tropical storm or hurricane conditions to landmasses within 48\xc2\xa0hours. Such systems are termed "potential tropical cyclones". Advisories on these storms contain the same content, including track forecasts and cyclone watches and warnings, as advisories on active tropical cyclones.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first storm to receive this designation was Potential Tropical Cyclone Two, which later developed into\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">\n        Tropical Storm Bret\n       </a>\n       , east-southeast of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">\n        Windward Islands\n       </a>\n       on June\xc2\xa018.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the numbering that a potential tropical cyclone receives would be retained for the rest of the hurricane season, meaning that the next tropical system would be designated with the following number, even though potential tropical cyclones do not qualify as tropical cyclones. This was first demonstrated with\n       <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Other_systems" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        Potential Tropical Cyclone Ten\n       </a>\n       , which failed to develop into a tropical cyclone.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n      <tr>\n        <td colspan="6" style="text-align:center;">\n         \xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td align="left">\n        </td>\n        <td align="left">\n         <b>\n          Actual activity\n         </b>\n         <br/>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         17\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         10\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         6\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="5" style="text-align:left;">\n         * June\xe2\x80\x93November only.\n         <br/>\n         \xe2\x80\xa0 Most recent of several such occurrences. (\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_Atlantic_hurricane_records#Seasonal_activity" title="List of Atlantic hurricane records">\n          See all\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Ahead of and during the season, several national meteorological services and scientific agencies forecast how many named storms, hurricanes and major (Category\xc2\xa03 or higher on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">\n        Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale\n       </a>\n       ) hurricanes will form during a season and/or how many tropical cyclones will affect a particular country. These agencies include the Tropical Storm Risk (TSR) Consortium of the University College London, the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">\n        National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration\n       </a>\n       (NOAA) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">\n        Colorado State University\n       </a>\n       (CSU). The forecasts include weekly and monthly changes in significant factors that help determine the number of tropical storms, hurricanes, and major hurricanes within a particular year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some of these forecasts also take into consideration what happened in previous seasons and the dissipation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event">\n        2014\xe2\x80\x9316 El Ni\xc3\xb1o event\n       </a>\n       . On average, an Atlantic hurricane season between 1981 and 2010 contained twelve tropical storms, six hurricanes, and two major hurricanes, with an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">\n        Accumulated Cyclone Energy\n       </a>\n       (ACE) index of between 66 and 103\xc2\xa0units.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Background_5-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Background-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-season_outlooks">\n        Pre-season outlooks\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-season outlooks">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The first forecast for the year was issued by TSR on December 13, 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They anticipated that the 2017 season would be a near-average season, with a prediction of 14 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes. They also predicted an ACE index of around 101\xc2\xa0units.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dec17TSR_6-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dec17TSR-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On December 14, CSU released a qualitative discussion detailing five possible scenarios for the 2017 season, taking into account the state of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Multidecadal_Oscillation" title="Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation">\n        Atlantic Multidecadal Oscillation\n       </a>\n       and the possibility of\n       <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o">\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o\n       </a>\n       developing during the season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dec17CSU_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Dec17CSU-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       TSR lowered their forecast numbers on April 5, 2017 to 11 named storms, 4 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes, based on recent trends favoring the development of El Ni\xc3\xb1o.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr17TSR_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Apr17TSR-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The next day, CSU released their prediction, also predicting a total of 11 named storms, 4 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr17CSU_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Apr17CSU-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On April 17,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Weather_Company" title="The Weather Company">\n        The Weather Company\n       </a>\n       released their forecasts, calling for 2017 to be a near-average season, with a total of 12 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr17TWC_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Apr17TWC-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The next day, on April 18,\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_State_University" title="North Carolina State University">\n        North Carolina State University\n       </a>\n       released their prediction, also predicting a near-average season, with a total of 11\xe2\x80\x9315 named storms, 4\xe2\x80\x936 hurricanes, and 1\xe2\x80\x933 major hurricanes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Apr17NCSU_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Apr17NCSU-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On May 20, The Weather Company issued an updated forecast, raising their numbers to 14 named storms, 7 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes to account for Tropical Storm Arlene as well as the decreasing chance of El Ni\xc3\xb1o forming during the season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May17TWC_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-May17TWC-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On May 25, NOAA released their prediction, citing a 70% chance of an above average season due to "a weak or nonexistent El Ni\xc3\xb1o", calling for 11\xe2\x80\x9317 named storms, 5\xe2\x80\x939 hurricanes, and 2\xe2\x80\x934 major hurricanes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOAA-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On May 26, TSR updated its prediction to around the same numbers as its December 2016 prediction, with only a minor change in the expected ACE index amount to 98\xc2\xa0units.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-May17TSR_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-May17TSR-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-season_outlooks">\n        Mid-season outlooks\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mid-season outlooks">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       CSU updated their forecast on June 1 to include 14 named storms, 6 hurricanes, and 2 major hurricanes, to include Tropical Storm Arlene.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-June17CSU_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-June17CSU-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was based on the current status of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Oscillation" title="North Atlantic Oscillation">\n        North Atlantic Oscillation\n       </a>\n       , which was showing signs of leaning towards a negative phase, favoring a warmer tropical Atlantic; and the chances of El Ni\xc3\xb1o forming were significantly lower. However, they stressed on the uncertainty that the\n       <a href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o%E2%80%93Southern_Oscillation" title="El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation">\n        El Ni\xc3\xb1o\xe2\x80\x93Southern Oscillation\n       </a>\n       could be in a warm-neutral phase or weak El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions by the peak of the season.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-June17CSU_14-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-June17CSU-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the same day, the United Kingdom\n       <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">\n        Met Office\n       </a>\n       (UKMO) released its forecast of a very slightly above-average season. It predicted 13 named storms, with a 70% chance that the number would be in the range between 10 and 16, and 8 hurricanes, with a 70% chance that the number would be in the range between 6 and 10. It also predicted an ACE index of 145, with a 70% chance that the index would be between 92 and 198.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-June17UKMO_15-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-June17UKMO-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On July 4, TSR released their fourth forecast for the season, increasing their predicted numbers to 17 named storms, 7 hurricanes, and 3 major hurricanes, due to the fact that El Ni\xc3\xb1o conditions would no longer develop by the peak of the season and the warming of sea-surface temperatures across the basin. Additionally, they predicted a revised ACE index of 116\xc2\xa0units.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jul17TSR_16-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jul17TSR-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During August 9, NOAA released their final outlook for the season, raising their predictions to 14\xe2\x80\x9319 named storms, though retaining 5\xe2\x80\x939 hurricanes and 2\xe2\x80\x935 major hurricanes. They also stated that the season had the potential to be extremely active, possibly the most active since\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2010 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2010\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_midOutlook_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NOAA_midOutlook-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">\n        Seasonal summary\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        Timeline of the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <center>\n       <div class="timeline-wrapper">\n        <map id="timeline_a0c40beb233df800c9f7450db0cb2ec3" name="timeline_a0c40beb233df800c9f7450db0cb2ec3">\n         <area alt="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)" coords="558,96,660,117" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ophelia_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Ophelia (2017)"/>\n         <area alt="Hurricane Nate (2017)" coords="538,84,624,104" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Nate_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Nate (2017)"/>\n         <area alt="Hurricane Maria" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Katia (2017)"/>\n         <area alt="Hurricane Jose (2017)" coords="491,33,577,53" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)"/>\n         <area alt="Hurricane Irma" coords="463,20,550,41" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Irma"/>\n         <area alt="Hurricane Harvey" coords="433,7,530,28" Franklin"/>\n         <area alt="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)" coords="239,33,330,53" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)"/>\n         <area coords="602,173,761,193" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale"/>\n        </map>\n        <img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/a0c40beb233df800c9f7450db0cb2ec3.png" usemap="#timeline_a0c40beb233df800c9f7450db0cb2ec3"/>\n       </div>\n      </center>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katia,_Irma,_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5175" data-file-width="9200" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/330px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/495px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg/660px-Katia%2C_Irma%2C_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg 2x" width="330"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katia,_Irma,_Jose_2017-09-08_1745Z%E2%80%931935Z.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Three simultaneous hurricanes active on September 8, with\n         <a href="#Hurricane_Katia">\n          Katia\n         </a>\n         <i>\n          (left)\n         </i>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">\n          Irma\n         </a>\n         <i>\n          (center)\n         </i>\n         , and\n         <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">\n          Jose\n         </a>\n         <i>\n          (right)\n         </i>\n         . All three were threatening land at the time.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Atlantic hurricane season officially began on June 1, 2017, although activity began earlier for the third consecutive year since\n       <a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2015\n       </a>\n       . Roughly a month before the official start, the first storm,\n       <a href="#TS_Arlene">\n        Arlene\n       </a>\n       , developed on April 19 in the northern Atlantic Ocean. It was the first named storm to develop in the month of April since\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">\n        Ana in 2003\n       </a>\n       . In June, two more tropical storms developed:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">\n        Bret\n       </a>\n       , which affected areas in the southeastern Caribbean Sea, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">\n        Trinidad and Tobago\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">\n        Cindy\n       </a>\n       , which formed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       less than a day after Bret had developed. In July, a tropical depression developed in the Main Development Region (MDR), the second tropical cyclone to develop in the MDR before the month of August, after Bret, and was followed by Tropical Storm Don. At the end of that month, a cold front stalled over the Gulf of Mexico and portions of the southeastern United States, spawning Tropical Depression Six, which quickly developed into Tropical Storm Emily.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhc_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       August featured the season\'s first hurricane, Franklin, which formed in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Campeche" title="Bay of Campeche">\n        Bay of Campeche\n       </a>\n       . A few days after Franklin dissipated, Tropical Storm Gert formed northeast of the Bahamas, eventually becoming a hurricane at a high latitude over the western Atlantic. On August 17,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Tropical Storm Harvey\n       </a>\n       formed east of the Windward Islands, before opening up into a wave over the central Caribbean three days later. Harvey then regenerated into a tropical depression over the southwestern Gulf of Mexico on August 23, and rapidly strengthened into a Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane before making landfall near\n       <a href="/wiki/Rockport,_Texas" title="Rockport, Texas">\n        Rockport, Texas\n       </a>\n       , late on August 25. Harvey became the first major hurricane to make landfall in the United States since Wilma in 2005, the first Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane to make landfall in Texas since Carla in 1961, and the first Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane landfall in the contiguous United States since\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Charley" title="Hurricane Charley">\n        Charley\n       </a>\n       in 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhc_22-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; clear: class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Tracks_from_2017_with_Precipitation_and_Cloud_Data.webm" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         2017 Atlantic Hurricane storm tracks with IMERG precipitation and GOES clouds (from August\xc2\xa010 to September\xc2\xa023).\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       September featured copious activity. Irma formed in the Eastern Atlantic and rapidly intensified into a Category\xc2\xa05 hurricane east of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">\n        Leeward Islands\n       </a>\n       . Irma is the strongest hurricane in terms of sustained winds since\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Wilma\n       </a>\n       in 2005, and the strongest hurricane outside of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">\n        Caribbean Sea\n       </a>\n       and Gulf of Mexico on record. While Irma impacted the northern Leeward Islands, Hurricane Jose formed on September 5, peaking as a high-end Category\xc2\xa04 hurricane before weakening and making an anti-cyclonic loop in the northern Atlantic Ocean. When Katia formed, 2017 became the first year since\n       <a href="/wiki/1998_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1998 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1998\n       </a>\n       in which six hurricanes have formed in a row.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On September 17, Maria became a Category\xc2\xa05 hurricane, threatening the same areas devastated by Hurricane Irma. When Lee intensified into a major hurricane on September 27, it became the first time in seven years that five major hurricanes formed. Activity briefly paused as September came to a close.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Activity resumed on October 4, when Tropical Depression Sixteen formed in the Southwestern Caribbean Sea, which strengthened into Tropical Storm Nate on the next day as it neared the coast of Nicaragua. Nate strengthened to a hurricane on October 7, and made two landfalls in the United States as a Category 1 hurricane - the first near the mouth of the Mississippi River in southeastern Louisiana late on October 7 and the second near Biloxi, Mississippi early October 8. As Nate became a post-tropical cyclone on October 9, Tropical Depression Seventeen formed in the eastern subtropical Atlantic, strengthening into Tropical Storm Ophelia that same day. Ophelia became a hurricane two days later, marking the first time since\n       <a href="/wiki/1893_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1893 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1893\n       </a>\n       that 10 consecutive named storms strengthened into hurricanes. On October 14, Ophelia unexpectedly strengthened into a major hurricane, becoming the sixth major hurricane of the season and the easternmost major hurricane in the Atlantic basin on record. After this, the basin went quiet for some time. Late in the month, Tropical Storm Philippe formed south of Cuba.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">\n        accumulated cyclone energy\n       </a>\n       (ACE) index for the 2017 Atlantic hurricane season, as of 21:00\xc2\xa0UTC on November\xc2\xa07, is 221.8525\xc2\xa0units,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [nb 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which is one of the highest values on record for an Atlantic hurricane season as well as the most since 2005, and more than double the 1981\xe2\x80\x932010 full-season median of 92 units. ACE is, broadly speaking, a measure of the power of the hurricane multiplied by the length of time it existed, so storms that last a long time, as well as particularly strong hurricanes, have high ACEs. It is only calculated for full advisories on tropical systems at or exceeding 39\xc2\xa0mph (63\xc2\xa0km/h), which is tropical storm strength. With an ACE value under 4\xc2\xa0units following the dissipation of Emily, 2017 set the record for lowest ACE produced by a season\'s first five named storms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FirstFive_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FirstFive-28">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite that, the 2017 season hosted the storm with the third-highest ACE value (Hurricane Irma, at 66.6 units) and is one of only four seasons (including\n       <a href="/wiki/1966_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1966 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        1966\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2003 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2003\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/2004_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2004 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2004\n       </a>\n       ) to have at least two hurricanes with an ACE value over 40 and the only season to have had three.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACE40three_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ACE40three-29">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       2017 also hosted the day with the most ACE produced (September 8) and currently has the\n       <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy#Atlantic_basin_ACE" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">\n        fourth highest ACE value of any Atlantic season since 1950\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nhc_22-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nhc-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       September also generated the highest ACE value for any month in the Atlantic, surpassing September\xc2\xa02004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">\n        Systems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Systems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Arlene">\n        Tropical Storm Arlene\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Arlene">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">\n         Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="Arlene 2017-04-20 1512Z.jpg" data-file-height="3600" data-file-width="2700" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/150px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/225px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg/300px-Arlene_2017-04-20_1512Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arlene_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="Arlene 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/150px-Arlene_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/225px-Arlene_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Arlene_2017_track.png/300px-Arlene_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         April 19\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 April 21\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         990\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes">\n        List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A potent\n       <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">\n        extratropical cyclone\n       </a>\n       formed well east of Bermuda on April\xc2\xa016. The cyclone moved southeast, becoming disconnected from the surrounding environment and gradually losing its frontal characteristics. Deep\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">\n        convection\n       </a>\n       formed in\n       <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">\n        bands\n       </a>\n       north and east of the center by 00:00\xc2\xa0UTC on April\xc2\xa019, leading to the formation of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">\n        subtropical depression\n       </a>\n       . Despite an unfavorable environment, with ocean temperatures near 20\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (68\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) and moderate\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">\n        wind shear\n       </a>\n       , convection coalesced near the center and allowed the subtropical depression to become fully tropical by 00:00\xc2\xa0UTC on April\xc2\xa020. It intensified into Tropical Storm Arlene six hours later. After attaining peak winds of 50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h), the storm began to rotate around a larger extratropical low. The storm tracked into the cold sector of the cyclone, causing Arlene to lose tropical characteristics around 12:00\xc2\xa0UTC on April\xc2\xa021. The post-tropical cyclone moved south and east, before dissipating well west-southwest of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">\n        Azores\n       </a>\n       on April\xc2\xa022.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Upon its formation as a subtropical depression on April\xc2\xa019, Arlene was the sixth known subtropical or tropical cyclone to form in the month of\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Atlantic hurricanes">\n        April\n       </a>\n       in the Atlantic basin; the other instances were Ana in 2003, a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_One_(1992)" title="Subtropical Storm One (1992)">\n        subtropical storm in April 1992\n       </a>\n       , and three tropical depressions in 1912, 1915, and 1973, respectively. When Arlene became a tropical storm on April\xc2\xa020, this marked only the second such occurrence on record, after Ana in 2003.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TWC-32">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [nb 3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Furthermore, it had the lowest central pressure of any Atlantic storm recorded in the month of April, with a central pressure of 990\xc2\xa0mbar (hPa; 29.23\xc2\xa0inHg), again surpassing Ana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, unrelated to Arlene,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2017_PHS#Tropical_Storm_Adrian" title="2017 PHS">\n        Tropical Storm Adrian\n       </a>\n       in the Eastern Pacific basin also formed before the corresponding hurricane season was set to officially begin, being the earliest named storm in the Eastern Pacific proper. This makes 2017 the second consecutive year after\n       <a href="/wiki/2016_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2016 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2016\n       </a>\n       where the first storms in both basins were pre-season storms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Bret">\n        Tropical Storm Bret\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Bret">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">\n         Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bret_2017-06-19_Suomi_NPP.jpg">\n            <img alt="Bret 2017-06-19 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="3175" data-file-width="2265" height="210"      <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         June 19\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 June 20\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         1007\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (2017)">\n        Tropical Storm Bret (2017)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">\n        tropical wave\n       </a>\n       moved off the coast of\n       <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">\n        Africa\n       </a>\n       on June 13 and was first monitored by the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">\n        National Hurricane Center\n       </a>\n       shortly afterwards.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Development, however, was expected to be slow due to its low latitude and relatively fast motion. As it moved swiftly across the Main Development Region of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       , the disturbance began to gradually organize, and the NHC raised development chances slightly on June 16.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Little change in organization occurred until June 18, at which point a burst of\n       <a href="/wiki/Convection" title="Convection">\n        convection\n       </a>\n       near the center of the disturbance prompted the NHC to designate the system as Potential Tropical Cyclone Two at 21:00\xc2\xa0UTC. This was the agency\'s first designation of a disturbance that had not yet developed into a tropical cyclone.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm continued to organize as it accelerated towards\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       and Trinidad and Tobago throughout the night, with banding features becoming evident. Later on June 19, the system developed a closed low-level circulation and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Bret at 21:00\xc2\xa0UTC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One day later, at 21:00\xc2\xa0UTC on June 20, the last advisory on Bret was issued following its degeneration into a tropical wave.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to Phil Klotzbach of Colorado State University, Bret was the earliest storm to form in the Main Development Region on record, surpassing a record set by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(1979)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (1979)">\n        Tropical Storm Ana\n       </a>\n       in 1979.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Bret was also the lowest latitude named storm in the month of June since\n       <a href="/wiki/1933_Trinidad_hurricane" title="1933 Trinidad hurricane">\n        1933\n       </a>\n       at 9.4\xc2\xb0N.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad" title="Trinidad">\n        Trinidad\n       </a>\n       , one person died after he slipped and fell while running across a makeshift bridge; the fatality is considered indirectly related to Bret.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another fatality occurred in Tobago after a man\'s house collapsed on him; he eventually succumbed to his injuries a week later.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Cindy">\n        Tropical Storm Cindy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Cindy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">\n         Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="Cindy 2017-06-21 1645Z.jpg" data-file-height="6400" data-file-width="5000" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/150px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/225px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg/300px-Cindy_2017-06-21_1645Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cindy_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="Cindy 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="3000" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/150px-Cindy_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/225px-Cindy_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Cindy_2017_track.png/300px-Cindy_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         June 20\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 June 23\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         60\xc2\xa0mph (95\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         992\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Cindy_(2017)" title="Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)">\n        Tropical Storm Cindy (2017)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The NHC first began monitoring the potential for tropical cyclone formation over the northwestern Caribbean Sea on June\xc2\xa013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A large area of disturbed weather developed within the region three days later,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and it slowly organized while entering the central Gulf of Mexico, prompting the NHC to begin advisories on a potential tropical cyclone on June\xc2\xa019. The structure of the system was initially sprawling, with tropical storm-force winds well displaced from a broad area of low pressure with embedded swirls.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system around 18:00\xc2\xa0UTC the following day was able to pinpoint a well-defined center, indicating the formation of Tropical Storm Cindy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite the presence of dry air and strong wind shear, the cyclone still managed to attain peak winds of 60\xc2\xa0mph (95\xc2\xa0km/h) before weakening on approach to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </a>\n       coastline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It made landfall between\n       <a href="/wiki/Port_Arthur,_Texas" title="Port Arthur, Texas">\n        Port Arthur, Texas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cameron,_Louisiana" title="Cameron, Louisiana">\n        Cameron, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       early on June\xc2\xa022 and weakened while progressing inland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A state of emergency was declared for\n       <a href="/wiki/Biloxi,_Mississippi" title="Biloxi, Mississippi">\n        Biloxi, Mississippi\n       </a>\n       in anticipation of flooding. A ten-year-old boy died from injuries sustained during the storm in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Morgan,_Alabama" title="Fort Morgan, Alabama">\n        Fort Morgan, Alabama\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A second fatality later occurred in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bolivar_Peninsula,_Texas" title="Bolivar Peninsula, Texas">\n        Bolivar Peninsula, Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Four">\n        Tropical Depression Four\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Four">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">\n         Tropical depression\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="04L 2017-07-06 1605Z.jpg" data-file-height="8601" data-file-width="6488" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/150px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/225px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg/300px-04L_2017-07-06_1605Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:04L_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="04L 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/150px-04L_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/225px-04L_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/04L_2017_track.png/300px-04L_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         July 5\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 7\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         30\xc2\xa0mph (45\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         1009\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Early on June\xc2\xa029, the NHC began tracking a tropical wave embedded within a large envelope of deep moisture across the coastline of western Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The disturbance was introduced as a potential contender for tropical cyclone formation two days later, as environmental conditions were expected to favor slow organization.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It began to show signs of organization over the central Atlantic early on July\xc2\xa03,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but the chances for development began to decrease two days later as the system moved toward a more stable environment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Having already acquired a well-defined circulation, the development of a persistent mass of deep convection around 03:00\xc2\xa0UTC the following day prompted the NHC to upgrade the wave to Tropical Depression Four, located about 1,545\xc2\xa0miles (2,485\xc2\xa0km) east of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">\n        Lesser Antilles\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Despite wind shear being low, the nascent depression struggled to intensify due to a dry environment caused by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Air_Layer" title="Saharan Air Layer">\n        Saharan Air Layer\n       </a>\n       to its east, causing the low-level circulation to weaken, and resulting in the tropical depression degenerating into an open tropical wave late on the next day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Don">\n        Tropical Storm Don\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Don">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">\n         Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="Don 2017-07-18 1718Z.jpg" data-file-height="3472" data-file-width="2672" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/150px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/225px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg/300px-Don_2017-07-18_1718Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Don_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="Don 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/150px-Don_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/225px-Don_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Don_2017_track.png/300px-Don_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         July 17\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 July 19\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         1007\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Late on July\xc2\xa015, the NHC highlighted a low-pressure trough over the central Atlantic as having the potential to develop into a tropical cyclone in the coming days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The disturbance began to show signs of organization early on July\xc2\xa017,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and data from a reconnaissance aircraft investigating the system confirmed the development of Tropical Storm Don around 21:00\xc2\xa0UTC that day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm\'s overall appearance improved over subsequent hours up until around 09:00 UTC, as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">\n        central dense overcast\n       </a>\n       , accompanied by significant clusters of lightning, became pronounced.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-64">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Don attained its peak intensity at this time, characterised by winds of approximately 50\xc2\xa0mph (85\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-:0-64">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The next plane to investigate the cyclone a few hours later, however, found that the system\'s center had become less defined, and that sustained wind speeds had decreased to about 40\xc2\xa0mph (65\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A combination of reconnaissance data and surface observations from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">\n        Windward Islands\n       </a>\n       indicated that Don opened up into a tropical wave around 03:00\xc2\xa0UTC on July\xc2\xa019, as it entered the eastern Caribbean Sea.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Emily">\n        Tropical Storm Emily\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Emily">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">\n         Tropical storm\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="Emily 2017-07-31 1555Z.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3000" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/150px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/225px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg/300px-Emily_2017-07-31_1555Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emily_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="Emily 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/150px-Emily_2017_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/225px-Emily_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Emily_2017_track.png/300px-Emily_2017_track.png 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Duration\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         July 31\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 August 2\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Peak intensity\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h)\n         <small>\n          (1-min)\n         </small>\n         1005\n         <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n          mbar\n         </a>\n         (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">\n          hPa\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In late July, a dissipating\n       <a href="/wiki/Cold_front" title="Cold front">\n        cold front\n       </a>\n       extended into the northeastern Gulf of Mexico, where the NHC began forecasting the development of an area of low pressure over the next day on July\xc2\xa030. Any development was expected to be slow due to land proximity and marginal upper-level winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Contrary to predictions, a rapid period of organization occurred over the next 24 hours and the system was deemed as Tropical Depression Six at 09:00\xc2\xa0UTC on July\xc2\xa031,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       strengthening into Tropical Storm Emily just two hours later. After attaining its peak intensity with winds of 45\xc2\xa0mph (75\xc2\xa0km/h) and a minimum pressure of 1,005\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millibar" title="Millibar">\n        mbar\n       </a>\n       (29.7\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inches_of_mercury" title="Inches of mercury">\n        inHg\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Emily made landfall on\n       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Island" title="Anna Maria Island">\n        Anna Maria Island\n       </a>\n       around 14:45\xc2\xa0UTC. Weakening quickly ensued, and later that day the circulation of Emily became elongated as it was downgraded to a tropical depression.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The increasingly disrupted system later moved off the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_Coast" title="First Coast">\n        First Coast\n       </a>\n       of Florida into the western Atlantic early the next day, accelerating northeastwards before becoming embedded within a frontal zone early on August\xc2\xa02.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the classification of Tropical Storm Emily, Florida Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">\n        Rick Scott\n       </a>\n       declared a\n       <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">\n        state of emergency\n       </a>\n       for 31\xc2\xa0counties to ensure residents were provided with the necessary resources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm spawned an EF0 tornado near Bradenton. The tornado was on the ground for about 1.3\xc2\xa0mi (2.1\xc2\xa0km) and destroyed two barns and a few greenhouses, while an engineered wall collapsed, leaving about $96,000 in damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On August\xc2\xa01, torrential rains related to Emily impacted parts of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miami_Beach" title="Miami Beach">\n        Miami Beach\n       </a>\n       , with accumulations reaching 6.97\xc2\xa0in (177\xc2\xa0mm) in 3.5\xc2\xa0hours, of which 2.17\xc2\xa0in (55\xc2\xa0mm) fell in just 30\xc2\xa0minutes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Coinciding with high tide the deluge overwhelmed flood pumps, with three of them shutting down due to lightning-induced power outages, and resulted in significant flash floods. Multiple buildings suffered water damage, with some having 2.5\xc2\xa0ft (0.76\xc2\xa0m) of standing water. One person was hospitalized after becoming stuck in flood waters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Portions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Downtown_Miami" title="Greater Downtown Miami">\n        Downtown Miami\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Brickell" title="Brickell">\n        Brickell\n       </a>\n       , were also heavily affected; numerous vehicles became stranded in flooded roadways.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Franklin">\n        Hurricane Franklin\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Hurricane Franklin">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">\n         Category 1\xc2\xa0hurricane\xc2\xa0(SSHWS)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <div style="vertical-align: middle">\n          <span class="nowrap">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg">\n            <img alt="Franklin 2017-08-09 1854Z.jpg" data-file-height="3480" data-file-width="2501" height="209" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg/300px-Franklin_2017-08-09_1854Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/>\n           </a>\n           <span class="nowrap">\n           </span>\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franklin_2017_track.png">\n            <img alt="Franklin 2017 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93"
